Buse, Billy Pacer aces 

N EW YORK (AFO — One is smooth as silk. the other rough as sandpaper. 
Together. Billy Knight and Don Buse are keeping the Indiana Pacers within hailing distance of the .5oo mark. 
That may not sound like much, but it s a lot better than the Pacers wore expected to do in their first National 
Basketball Association season. 
“ A lot of the guys were insulted when they read all that stuff about how we were tile weakest of the four new teams and how we wouldn’t do well,” said Buse. who rarely lets a game go by without coming up with some new floor burns from diving after loose balls. “ You don't like to read that you’re the worst team in the league.” 
ABA survivor 

The Pacers, one of four teams ab­ sorbed from the American Basketball 
Association, have shown they are far from the worst team in the league, compiling a respectable 27-34 record to rank fourth in the six-team Midwest 
Division despite Saturday night’s 
129-115 loss to the New York Knicks— 
Indiana’s loth straight road defeat. 
But the Pacers still have a recogni­ tion problem. 
“ Many people in NBA cities are not fam iliar with our p layers.” says 
Indiana Coach Bobby “ Slick” Leonard. 
“ but that can work to our advantage. 
We have some talented players here, and sometimes we can sneak up on people ’’ 
Or as Buse says of his own identiy crisis. * * VV hat thief wants to be well-known?” 

Well. Buse is going to have a hard time maintaining a low profile after the season he’s having. He leads the league in steals and assists, averaging 
3.3 steals and 8.7 assists per game. 
Theft traits 
Buse says his steals are a result of his quick hands and his ability to anti­ cipate passes and moves, while the assists come from his role in the In­ diana offense. “ I handle the ball 9o per cent of the time, and when we’re run­ ning I ’m going to get my assists.” the rugged 26-year-old backcourt man said. 
A scorer in high school, where his idol was Cazzie Russell, and college. where he guided Evan sville to the 
NCAA Division ll title. Buse has been asked so many times about his transi­ tion to plavmaker that he’s developed a catchy response. 
“ When I broke into the lineup we had 
George McGinnis at one forward and 
Billy Knight at the other.” his routine goes. “ They said to me, ‘Listen, you’re gonna have to learn how to do someth­ ing besides shoot, because we’re gonna do all the shooting around here.’ So I realized that if I wanted to play. I ’d better learn how to pass.” 
McGinnis, who went to Philadelphia 
H i years ago, says he misses Buse. 
Respect 
“ He’s a heck of a player,” says Big 
George. “ I think he’s the most solid guard in the league. He definitely has the quickest hands. If we had Buse. we d win 7o games.” 
Knight, meanwhile, is happy Buse is 

 still in Indiana 
“ Buse is the reason I ’m having such a great year.” says Knight. “ There s no player I ’d rather be with than him. 
If he was ever traded. I hope I ’d go too in a package deal.” 
That’s not likely to happen. Indian­ a’s whole offense is built around Buse bringing the ball upcourt anc] getting it to Knight, who is a threat to score from 
.anywhere inside 2o feet. An all-star forward in the ABA last year, Knight was shifted to guard for the first half of this season, then returned to the front line when the Pacers obtained John 
Williamson from the Nets. 
‘‘The change in positions really didn’t m atter, since I was playing pretty much the same game either w ay.” the 6-6 Knight explained. “ I would shoot from the corners, use my moves to get free and go to the boards." 
Knight's game is built around his moves, a dazzling array which have helped him to a 26.8 scoring average, third-best in the league. 
“ I ’m quicker than most of the for­ wards I play ag ain st.” said the 
24-year-old, third-year pro from Pitt, 
“ but they may have an edge in size and strength. So I have to put on moves and fake them out of position before I can get off my shots.” 

While Buse is a hard-nosed player who shows his emotions, the bearded 
Knight is Mr. Cool on the court. 
“ I try never to lost my cool,” said 
Knight. “ I ’m not an aggressive person, and I think it would hurt my game if! showed my emotions.”

K opay says 
NFL has many homosexuals 

NEW 5 ORK (AP) — David Kopay, the former running hack who has admitted a sexual preference for men, said Monday that the National Football 
League has a large number of homo­ sexuals "hiding behind a wall of si­ ll-nee." 
"People would fall over in shock if the names were ever disclosed." the 
B-foot-1 inch, 2o3-pound veteran of IO years in the NTL added. 
"I have talked to some of them since 
I made my revelation more than a year ago. Most of them are supportive of my action but are afraid to do the same. 
They act edgy and frightened as if to say, ‘Oh. my God, you’ve gotten too close to home." 
Kopay, now a resident of Washing­ ton. D. C., came to New York to promote his book. "The David Kopay 
Story.” described as "an extraordin­ ary self-revelation.” 
Book 
His advance on the book, which a l­ ready has gone into three printings and has been sold to a paper back distri­ butor. reaches into six figures, he said, and negotiations are being made for movie rights. 
In the book. Kopay reveals that his first homosexual experience was with a fraternity brother while an under­ graduate at the 
U niversity of 
Washington. He said that, while serv­ ing on specialty teams with six NFL clubs, he dated both men and women. 
"I was uptight as hell." he acknow­ ledged. " It was a long time before I admitted these feelings to myself. By the time I quit pro football, most of my friends knew." 

Kopay. now 34. first signed with the 
San Francisco 49ers in 1964. He played four years there, then hit Detroit, Wa­ shington. New Orleans, O akland, 
Green Bay and the Southern California 
Sun of the now defunct World Football 
League before retiring in 1974. 
"Since then I have been black-list­ ed." he said. "I felt I was qualified to be a coach or a scout on a pro team I wrote six teams. I received only one answer. It came from Bart S tarr, coach of the Green Bay Packers. 
"Starr is a decent guy. He at least answered. He said he thought highly of me but he had no position for me." 
Silence 
Kopav declined, for obvious reasons to reveal names, but said that more than five per cent of the NFL players were either homosexual or bisexual. 
He declined to confirm the report that three well-known quarterbacks are in­ cluded. 
He said his family had greeted his revelation with mixed emotions. "My dad threatened to kill m e," he said. 
"I ve got a younger brother with a wife and two kids who is not concerned at all. My sister is the same. My older brother is different. He is all wrapped up in that football macho stuff.” 
Kopay said he had decided to go open with his feelings because "this is the last area of discrimination to be dealt with." 
"It is a case of human rights," he added "It is parallel to ‘Roots,’ the discrim ination against blacks; the women’s movement and international civil rights. It represents the right to exist, work and love as you please."

San Antonio’s four remaining - high school basketball teams square off in two bidistrict clashes Tuesday night that will decided half the field for Sa­ turday’s four-team regional tourna­ ment in the Alamo City. 
The 
Judson 
Rockets, 
D istrict 
29-AAAA champions, will collide with the 
Kennedy 
Rockets. 
D istrict 
3o-A A AA kings, at 7:3o p.m. at Alamo 
Stadium Gym. 
In the other bidistrict m atchup, 
31-AAAA winner Burbank goes against the Lee Volunteers of 32-AAAA at 7:3o p.m. at Blossom Athletic Center. 
Area battles 

The two other bidistrict matchups in 
Region IV will also be conducted at 
7:3o p.m. Tuesday. 
Defending regional champion Vic­ toria (33-2) meets Austin Reagan 
(2o-11) at Texas Lutheran College in 
Seguin. 
Corpus Christi Moody (34-2). last, vear’s regional runnerup, tests 
Mission (26-9) at Edinburg High 
School. 
The Judson Rockets were the only one of the four district winners to win a title outright. They won all 12 district games. 18 of their last 19 and now stand 26-9. 
Rocket engines 

Two games they didn’t win. though. were against another Rocket team. 
Kennedy variety.. Kennedy ripped 
Judson twice. 77-68. in tho Alamo 
Heights Tourney Nov. 2o, then 71-48 on 
Dec. 3 in the South San Tournament during its 27-11 campaign. 

JFK is led by the high-scoring trio of 
.Darryl Bethlev (19.1). Rick Leggett 
(18.o) and Dale Roberson (15.3). The 
Leggett family will he busy Tuesday night, as older brother Roy will be trying to help St. M ary’s beat East 
Texas State. 
Judson’s scoring leaders are Joe 
Blake (13.9), and twins Stacy (13.3) and Tracy (12.1) Bowers. 
The Burbank-Lee clash matches the 
Nos. 1-2 ranked teams in the F.x- press-News weekly poll, with Burbank bringing a 31-4 mark against Lee’s 
26-9. They have not met. 
The game will match two of the top centers in the state. 6-11 Gilbert Salinr as of Burbank and 6-7 Chuck Stanley of 
Lee, so who stays out of foul trouble will bo important. 
Salinas, the city’s all-tim e career scoring leader who has a 2o.7 mark this year, returned to the starting lin­ eup last Saturday night and helped the 
Bulldogs nip Sam Houston, 6o-57. iii the district playoff. Without him. Bur­ bank lost three games by a total of nine points. 
Runnerup 
Stanley is the No. 2 scorer in the city this year with a 25.6 average. 
Both stars have plenty of help, as 
Steve Gamboa, Leonard Lambert. E r­ nest Puente and Mike Poole round out the starting cast for the Bulldogs and 
Lee has top players in Jeff Brown, Bill 
Bond, Jimmy Stewart and Ed flatten. 
Burbank went to regional last year. while Lee lost in a district playoff The 
Vols this year, though, heat Seguin. 
58-53, to win the loop, handing the Ma­ tadors half their six losses for the year.

SAC trailed 1o-o at the outset but rallied to take a 19-18 lead. A to p sy ­ turvy first half ended with Temple on top. 39-35. 
SAC took its final lead for the night at 51-49 before Temple unloaded eight straight pooints. four each by Danny 
Salisbury and Greg Crumpton. The 
Wildoats put away the victory with ll straight free throws toward the end. 
Billy Bailey. SAC’s leading scorer, had an ice-cold second half, hitting only one field goal. Bailey led SAC with 
14 points. 
"We came out a little tight tonight." said Culpepper, whose team beat 
Temple twice in regular season play. 
"We had lots of turnovers, hut we hit the bucket well in the firat half. 
‘ T e m p le s playoff experience helped." he added. " I think that was the difference. They were very poised in the second half. We got tighter and tired in the second half. They were mentally ready and we were mentally tired." 
Sun Jacinto, which went unbeaten in 
16 league games, found itself down 
63-54 tn the second hall before running off 18 straight {joints for a 72-63 lead 
Alton Lister, Arthur Ross and . .Ollie 
Mack had six points each during the surge. 

Lee came back to cut the gap to 79-75 but got no closer. Lee led. 51-48. at halftime. 
Lister, a 6-11 giant, had 32 points for the Ravens, who raised their season record to 27-5. Mack added 31 and Ken 
Logan had 18. Calvet Shelley led Lee with 22. 
Lee drops to 29-11 on the year. Tem­ ple is now 15-15 and SAC finishes with a 
14-16 mark.

Morris, 86-71. Monday night.

Thomas may be GM again 

BALTIMORE (AP) — An Ohio builder is about to buy controlling interest i ii the San Francisco 49ers lor 813 million and install fired Baltimore Colts’ official Joe Thomas as general manager of the 
National Football League team, it was reported 
Monday. 
The Baltimore News American, in a copyright**! story, said Edward J. DeBartolo, a contractor from 
Youngstown, Ohio, has won approval of both attorneys for the estates of the late Morabito brothers, founders of the team, and the 49ers’ minority stockholders. 
It said DeBartolo, a longtime friend of Thomas, was among four bidders for the franchise, with the other groups including comedian Bob Hope, Wayne 
V alley, former partner in the Oakland Raiders; Sam 
Schulman. owner of the National Basketball Asso- ciation Seattle Supersonics, and Albe Sherman, former coach of the New York Giants 
According to the News American. DeBartolo will reportedly pay more than $13 million for 8o per cent control of the 49ers The remaining 2o per cent will 
In* retained by the club's minority stockholders, the palier reported 
Thomas told the News American that he would not confirm the report, but hinted it was true 
“ Until the final details are worked out and the sale of the 49ers is approved by the league, it will not be official," he said 
Thomas was unavailable for further comment. 
In San Francisco, a 49ers spokesman refused to confirm or deny the report.

Fleas are pretty choosy in selecting their food source. They would real­ ly rather jump on the cat or the dog but will take humans if they are closer and the flea is quite hungry. Even then, fleas seem to prefer certain individuals in a fam ily over others. 
The so-called “ sand fle a s ", are really the common cat flea or dog flea The name is derived from the fact that they are often found out of 
(lftors. After the flea has had its meal of blood, it may drop off and rest for a while before hopping back on an animal. This means that an entire yard may have a scatter­ ing of fleas if your pet lives and travels over the whole yard area. 
It is quite possible to have fleas when you don’t have any pets at all. The neighbor's dog or cat may wander into your yard and leave you with a sprinkling of fleas. Fleas can also be carried in by raccoons, possums, and squirrels as well as rats and mice. 
Flea bites are painful and in some parts of the world they carry serious diseases, such as bubonic plague. To be free of the nuisance of fleas, and other pests, call Termin- i\ International now in

A fFruit Juice Break’ Makes 
Refreshing, Healthy Habit 

The saying “ There’s nothing new under the sun,’’ is really only half true. Th ere’s nothing new about vending ma­ chines and there’s noth­ ing new about canned fruit juices, hut when you put canned fruit juices in vending machines you have an innovative mer­ chandising idea that's turned into an entirely new business for hundreds of people who wish to work either part time or full tim e to supplement their in­ come. 
Century 
M arketing 
Corporation, headed by 
David Madden, is one of those new businesses that 
San Antonio has been trying to attract. Century is headquartered here in 
San 
Antonio with branches in 
Dallas. 
Houston. Freeport and 
Corpus Christi. Plans to open an office in Harlin­ gen is scheduled for the first part of 1977. 
There is nothing new about vending machines hut the four “ C’s " have dominated what the pub­ lic could purchase when hunger pangs set in. But the four “ C ’s” (coffee, coke, candy and cig ar­ ettes) are frowned upon by most doctors, so when naturally sweetened fruit juices were made availa­ ble in offices, hotels or anyplace one usually finds vending machines. 

 there was an instant consumer acceptance JI and Century Marketing was on its way to success. 
Madden stated that his m arketing philosophy was to offer people with limited capital an oppor­ tunity to go into business for themselves either on a full time basis or a part time basis. 
The distributors usual­ ly purchase five m a­ chines; Century offers the distributor a wide variety of locations, in­ stalls the machines and even helps the distributor service the machines. 
The average operator with five machines can make a profit of between 
$4(1o to $54o per month. At 
$54o per month that s a return on your invest­ ment of about 1o8%. 
Most distributors are businessmen, retired mi­ litary, teachers, and even housewives who want to supplement their in ­ comes. It takes about an hour and a half per week to service five machines and that's the great ap­ peal to a lot of distribu­ tors who want to ease themselves into their own successful business and eventually become their own boss. 
Madden says, “ For the health of your employees, give them the choice of healthy, naturally swee­ tened fruit juice, lf you
